<p>According to economists <a href="/wiki/Michael_Clemens" title="Michael Clemens">Michael Clemens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lant_Pritchett" title="Lant Pritchett">Lant Pritchett</a>, "permitting people to move from low-productivity places to high-productivity places appears to be by far the most efficient generalized policy tool, at the margin, for poverty reduction".<sup id="cite_ref-:82_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:82-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> A successful two-year <a href="/wiki/In_situ" title="In situ">in situ</a> anti-poverty program, for instance, helps poor people make in a year what is the equivalent of working one day in the developed world.<sup id="cite_ref-:82_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:82-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> A slight reduction in the barriers to labor mobility between the developing and developed world would do more to <a href="/wiki/Poverty_reduction" title="Poverty reduction">reduce poverty</a> in the developing world than any remaining trade liberalization.<sup id="cite_ref-WalmsleyWinters2005_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WalmsleyWinters2005-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research on a migration lottery allowing Tongans to move to New Zealand found that the lottery winners saw a 263% increase in income from migrating (after only one year in New Zealand) relative to the unsuccessful lottery entrants.<sup id="cite_ref-McKenzieStillman2010_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKenzieStillman2010-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> A longer-term study on the Tongan lottery winners finds that they "continue to earn almost 300 percent more than non-migrants, have better mental health, live in households with more than 250 percent higher expenditure, own more vehicles, and have more durable assets".<sup id="cite_ref-:9_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> A conservative estimate of their lifetime gain to migration is NZ$315,000 in net present value terms (approximately US$237,000).<sup id="cite_ref-:9_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2017 study of Mexican immigrant households in the United States found that by virtue of moving to the United States, the households increase their incomes more than fivefold immediately.<sup id="cite_ref-Gove2017_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gove2017-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> The study also found that the "average gains accruing to migrants surpass those of even the most successful current programs of economic development."<sup id="cite_ref-Gove2017_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gove2017-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2017 study of European migrant workers in the UK shows that upon accession to the EU, the migrant workers see a substantial positive impact on their earnings. The data indicate that acquiring EU status raises earnings for the workers by giving them the right to freely change jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-Ruhs2017_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ruhs2017-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2017 study in the <i><a href="/wiki/Quarterly_Journal_of_Economics" title="Quarterly Journal of Economics">Quarterly Journal of Economics</a></i> found that immigrants from middle- and low-income countries to the United States increased their wages by a factor of two to three upon migration.<sup id="cite_ref-HendricksSchoellman2018_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HendricksSchoellman2018-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Innovation_and_entrepreneurship">Innovation and entrepreneurship</span></h3>
<p>A 2017 survey of the existing economic literature found that "high-skilled migrants boost innovation and productivity outcomes."<sup id="cite_ref-KerrKerr2017_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KerrKerr2017-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> According to a 2013 survey of the existing economic literature, "much of the existing research points towards positive net contributions by immigrant entrepreneurs."<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Areas where immigrant are more prevalent in the United States have substantially more innovation (as measured by patenting and citations).<sup id="cite_ref-AkcigitGrigsby2017_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AkcigitGrigsby2017-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Immigrants to the United States create businesses at higher rates than natives.<sup id="cite_ref-KerrKerr2016_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KerrKerr2016-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> A 2010 study showed "that a 1 percentage point increase in immigrant college graduates' population share increases patents per capita by 9–18 percent."<sup id="cite_ref-HuntGauthier-Loiselle2010_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HuntGauthier-Loiselle2010-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Mass migration can also boost innovation and growth, as shown by the Jewish, Huguenot and Bohemian diasporas in Berlin and Prussia,<sup id="cite_ref-Hornung2014_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hornung2014-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hornung2018_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hornung2018-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-de_Vries2018_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de_Vries2018-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> German Jewish Émigrés in the US,<sup id="cite_ref-MoserVoena2014_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoserVoena2014-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> the Mariel boatlift,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> the exodus of Soviet Jews to Israel in the 1990s,<sup id="cite_ref-Razin2018_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Razin2018-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> European migration to Argentina during the Age of Mass Migration (1850–1914),<sup id="cite_ref-Droller2018_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Droller2018-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> west-east migration in the wake of German reunification,<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> and Polish immigration to Germany after joining the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> A 2018 study in the <i>Economic Journal</i> found that "that a 10% increase in immigration from exporters of a given product is associated with a 2% increase in the likelihood that the host country starts exporting that good ‘from scratch’ in the next decade."<sup id="cite_ref-BaharRapoport2018_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaharRapoport2018-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Immigrants have been linked to greater invention and innovation in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr2010_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr2010-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> According to one report, "immigrants have started more than half (44 of 87) of America's startup companies valued at $1 billion dollars or more and are key members of management or product development teams in over 70 percent (62 of 87) of these companies."<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> One analysis found that immigrant-owned firms had a higher innovation rate (on most measures of innovation) than firms owned by U.S.-born entrepreneurs.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> Research also shows that labor migration increases human capital.<sup id="cite_ref-DinkelmanMariotti2016_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinkelmanMariotti2016-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shrestha2017_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shrestha2017-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BeineDocquier2008_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeineDocquier2008-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BatistaLacuesta2012_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BatistaLacuesta2012-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Foreign doctoral students are a major source of innovation in the American economy.<sup id="cite_ref-StuenMobarak2012_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StuenMobarak2012-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> In the United States, immigrant workers hold a disproportionate share of jobs in science, technology, engineering, and math (STEM): "In 2013, foreign-born workers accounted for 19.2 percent of STEM workers with a bachelor's degree, 40.7 percent of those with a master's degree, and more than half—54.5 percent—of those with a Ph.D."<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Quality_of_institutions">Quality of institutions</span></h2>
<p>A 2015 study finds "some evidence that larger immigrant population shares (or inflows) yield positive impacts on institutional quality. At a minimum, our results indicate that no negative impact on economic freedom is associated with more immigration."<sup id="cite_ref-ClarkLawson2015_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ClarkLawson2015-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Another study, looking at the increase in Israel's population in the 1990s due to the unrestricted immigration of Jews from the Soviet Union, finds that the mass immigration did not undermine political institutions, and substantially increased the quality of economic institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> A 2017 study in the <i><a href="/wiki/British_Journal_of_Political_Science" title="British Journal of Political Science">British Journal of Political Science</a></i> argued that the British American colonies without slavery adopted better democratic institutions in order to attract migrant workers to their colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-Nikolova2015_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nikolova2015-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NikolovaNikolova2017_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NikolovaNikolova2017-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> A 2018 study fails to find evidence that immigration to the United States weakens economic freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-PadillaCachanosky2018_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PadillaCachanosky2018-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> A 2019 study of Jordan found that the massive influx of refugees into Jordan during the Gulf War had long-lasting positive effects on Jordanian economic institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Welfare">Welfare</span></h2>
<p>Some research has found that as immigration and ethnic heterogeneity increase, government funding of <a href="/wiki/Welfare" title="Welfare">welfare</a> and public support for welfare decrease.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schmidt-CatranSpies2016_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmidt-CatranSpies2016-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_nepotism" title="Ethnic nepotism">Ethnic nepotism</a> may be an explanation for this phenomenon. Other possible explanations include theories regarding <a href="/wiki/In-group" class="mw-redirect" title="In-group">in-group</a> and out-group effects and <a href="/wiki/Reciprocal_altruism" title="Reciprocal altruism">reciprocal altruism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Freeman2009_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freeman2009-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research however also challenges the notion that ethnic heterogeneity reduces public goods provision.<sup id="cite_ref-Wimmer2016_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wimmer2016-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KymlickaBanting2011_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KymlickaBanting2011-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Studies that find a negative relationship between ethnic diversity and public goods provision often fail to take into account that strong states were better at assimilating minorities, thus decreasing diversity in the long run.<sup id="cite_ref-Wimmer2016_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wimmer2016-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Ethnically diverse states today consequently tend to be weaker states.<sup id="cite_ref-Wimmer2016_217-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wimmer2016-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Because most of the evidence on fractionalization comes from sub-Saharan Africa and the United States, the generalizability of the findings is questionable.<sup id="cite_ref-KymlickaBanting2011_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KymlickaBanting2011-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> A 2018 study in the <i><a href="/wiki/American_Political_Science_Review" title="American Political Science Review">American Political Science Review</a></i> cast doubts on findings that ethnoracial homogeneity led to greater public goods provision.<sup id="cite_ref-KustovPardelli2018_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KustovPardelli2018-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research finds that Americans' attitudes towards immigration influence their attitudes towards welfare spending.<sup id="cite_ref-GarandXu2017_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GarandXu2017-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<p>A 2016 study found that immigration in the period 1940–2010 in the United States increased the high school completion of natives: "An increase of one percentage point in the share of immigrants in the population aged 11–64 increases the probability that natives aged 11–17 eventually complete 12 years of schooling by 0.3 percentage point."<sup id="cite_ref-Hunt2017_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hunt2017-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies have found that non-native speakers of English in the UK have no causal impact on the performance of other pupils,<sup id="cite_ref-GeayMcNally2013_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GeayMcNally2013-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> immigrant children have no significant impact on the test scores of Dutch children,<sup id="cite_ref-OhinataVan_Ours2013_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OhinataVan_Ours2013-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> no effect on grade repetition among native students exposed to migrant students in Austrian schools,<sup id="cite_ref-Schneeweis2015_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schneeweis2015-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> that the presence of Latin American children in schools had no significant negative effects on peers, but that students with limited English skills had slight negative effects on peers,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> and that the influx of Haitians to Florida public schools after the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a> had no effects on the educational outcomes of incumbent students.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2018 study found that the "presence of immigrant students who have been in the country for some time is found to have no effect on natives. However, a small negative effect of recent immigrants on natives’ language scores is reported."<sup id="cite_ref-Bossavie2018_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bossavie2018-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Another 2018 study found that the presence of immigrant students to Italy was associated with "small negative average effects on maths test scores that are larger for low ability native students, strongly non-linear and only observable in classes with a high (top 20%) immigrant concentration. These outcomes are driven by classes with a high average linguistic distance between immigrants and natives, with no apparent additional role played by ethnic diversity."<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Assimilation">Assimilation</span></h2>
<p>A 2019 review of existing research in the <i><a href="/wiki/Annual_Review_of_Sociology" title="Annual Review of Sociology">Annual Review of Sociology</a></i> on immigrant assimilation in the United States, the United Kingdom, France, Germany, Sweden, Norway, Belgium, the Netherlands and Spain concluded "we find an overall pattern of intergenerational assimilation in terms of socioeconomic attainment, social relations, and cultural beliefs."<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span></h3>
<p>A 2018 study in the <i>American Sociological Review</i> found that within racial groups, most immigrants to the United States had fully assimilated within a span of 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-VillarrealTamborini2018_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VillarrealTamborini2018-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Immigrants arriving in the United States after 1994 assimilate more rapidly than immigrants who arrived in previous periods.<sup id="cite_ref-VillarrealTamborini2018_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VillarrealTamborini2018-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Measuring assimilation can be difficult due to "ethnic attrition", which refers to when ancestors of migrants cease to self-identify with the nationality or ethnicity of their ancestors. This means that successful cases of assimilation will be underestimated. Research shows that ethnic attrition is sizable in Hispanic and Asian immigrant groups in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-DuncanTrejo2011_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DuncanTrejo2011-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AlbaIslam2008_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlbaIslam2008-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> By taking account of ethnic attrition, the assimilation rate of Hispanics in the United States improves significantly.<sup id="cite_ref-DuncanTrejo2011_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DuncanTrejo2011-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DuncanTrejo2016_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DuncanTrejo2016-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> A 2016 paper challenges the view that cultural differences are necessarily an obstacle to long-run economic performance of migrants. It finds that "first generation migrants seem to be less likely to success the more culturally distant they are, but this effect vanishes as time spent in the US increases."<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2018 study found that Chinese nationals in the United States who received permanent residency permits from the US government amid the Tianamen Square protests (and subsequent Chinese government clampdown) experienced significant employment and earnings gains relative to similar immigrant groups who did not have the same residency rights.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the Age of Mass Migration, infant arrivals to the United States had greater economic success over their lifetime than teenage arrivals.<sup id="cite_ref-AlexanderWard2018_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlexanderWard2018-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h3>
<p>A 2015 report by the National Institute of Demographic Studies finds that an overwhelming majority of second-generation immigrants of all origins in France feel French, despite the persistent discrimination in education, housing and employment that many of the minorities face.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research shows that country of origin matters for speed and depth of immigrant assimilation but that there is considerable assimilation overall.<sup id="cite_ref-Blau2015_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blau2015-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Research finds that first generation immigrants from countries with less egalitarian gender cultures adopt gender values more similar to natives over time.<sup id="cite_ref-RoderMuhlau2014_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RoderMuhlau2014-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spierings2014_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spierings2014-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> According to one study, "this acculturation process is almost completed within one generational succession: The gender attitudes of second generation immigrants are difficult to distinguish from the attitudes of members of mainstream society. This holds also for children born to immigrants from very gender traditional cultures and for children born to less well integrated immigrant families."<sup id="cite_ref-RoderMuhlau2014_237-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RoderMuhlau2014-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Similar results are found on a study of Turkish migrants to Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Spierings2014_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spierings2014-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> The assimilation on gender attitudes has been observed in education, as one study finds "that the female advantage in education observed among the majority population is usually present among second-generation immigrants."<sup id="cite_ref-FleischmannKristen2014_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FleischmannKristen2014-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Share_of_Migrants_in_the_world_2015-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Share_of_Migrants_in_the_world_2015-en.svg/260px-Share_of_Migrants_in_the_world_2015-en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Share_of_Migrants_in_the_world_2015-en.svg/390px-Share_of_Migrants_in_the_world_2015-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Share_of_Migrants_in_the_world_2015-en.svg/520px-Share_of_Migrants_in_the_world_2015-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1370" data-file-height="688" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Share_of_Migrants_in_the_world_2015-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Share of migrants in all countries. Data from 2015.</div></div></div>
<p>A 2017 study of Switzerland found that naturalization strongly improves long-term social integration of immigrants: "The integration returns to naturalization are larger for more marginalized immigrant groups and when naturalization occurs earlier, rather than later in the residency period."<sup id="cite_ref-HainmuellerHangartner2017_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HainmuellerHangartner2017-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> A separate study of Switzerland found that naturalization improved the economic integration of immigrants: "winning Swiss citizenship in the referendum increased annual earnings by an average of approximately 5,000 U.S. dollars over the subsequent 15 years. This effect is concentrated among more marginalized immigrants."<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>First-generation immigrants tend to hold less accepting views of homosexual lifestyles but opposition weakens with longer stays.<sup id="cite_ref-Röder2018_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Röder2018-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Second-generation immigrants are overall more accepting of homosexual lifestyles, but the acculturation effect is weaker for Muslims and to some extent, Eastern Orthodox migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-Röder2018_242-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Röder2018-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A study of Bangladeshi migrants in East London found they shifted towards the thinking styles of the wider non-migrant population in just a single generation.<sup id="cite_ref-CaldwellMesoudi2016_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaldwellMesoudi2016-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A study on Germany found that foreign-born parents are more likely to integrate if their children are entitled to German citizenship at birth.<sup id="cite_ref-AvitabileClots-Figueras2013_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvitabileClots-Figueras2013-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> A 2017 study found that "faster access to citizenship improves the economic situation of immigrant women, especially their labour market attachment with higher employment rates, longer working hours and more stable jobs. Immigrants also invest more in host country-specific skills like language and vocational training. Faster access to citizenship seems a powerful policy instrument to boost economic integration in countries with traditionally restrictive citizenship policies."<sup id="cite_ref-GathmannKeller2017_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GathmannKeller2017-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Naturalization" title="Naturalization">Naturalization</a> is associated with large and persistent wage gains for the naturalized citizens in most countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Gathmann2015_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gathmann2015-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> One study of Denmark found that providing immigrants with voting rights reduced their crime rate.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies on programs that randomly allocate refugee immigrants across municipalities find that the assignment of neighborhood impacts immigrant crime propensity, education and earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-DammDustmann2014_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DammDustmann2014-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ÅslundEdin2011_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ÅslundEdin2011-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Damm2014_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Damm2014-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Damm2009_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Damm2009-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EdinFredriksson2003_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EdinFredriksson2003-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JonesTeytelboym2018_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JonesTeytelboym2018-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> A 2019 study found that refugees who resettled in areas with many conationals were more likely to be economically integrated.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research suggests that bilingual schooling reduces barriers between speakers from two different communities.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research suggests that a vicious cycle of bigotry and isolation could reduce assimilation and increase bigotry towards immigrants in the long-term. For instance, University of California, San Diego political scientist Claire Adida, Stanford University political scientist David Laitin and Sorbonne University economist Marie-Anne Valfort argue "fear-based policies that target groups of people according to their religion or region of origin are counter-productive. Our own research, which explains the failed integration of Muslim immigrants in France, suggests that such policies can feed into a vicious cycle that damages national security. French Islamophobia—a response to cultural difference—has encouraged Muslim immigrants to withdraw from French society, which then feeds back into French Islamophobia, thus further exacerbating Muslims’ alienation, and so on. Indeed, the failure of French security in 2015 was likely due to police tactics that intimidated rather than welcomed the children of immigrants—an approach that makes it hard to obtain crucial information from community members about potential threats."<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A study which examined <a href="/wiki/Catalan_nationalism" title="Catalan nationalism">Catalan nationalism</a> examined the Catalan Government's policy towards the integration of immigrants during the start of the 1990s. At this time the Spanish region of Catalonia was experiencing a large influx in the number of immigrants from Northern Africa , Latin America and Asia.The Spanish government paid little attention to this influx of immigrants. However, Catalan politicians began discussing how the increase in immigrants would effect Catalan identity. Members of the Catalan parliament petitioned for a plan to integrate these immigrants into Catalan society. Crucially , the plan did not include policies regarding <a href="/wiki/Naturalization" title="Naturalization">naturalisation</a> , which were key immigration policies of the Spanish government.The plan of the Catalan parliament aimed to create a shared Catalan identity which included both the native Catalan population and immigrant communities. This meant that immigrants were encouraged to relate as part of the Catalan community but also encouraged to retain their own culture and traditions. In this way assimilation of immigrant cultures in Catalonia was avoided.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2018 study in the <i>British Journal of Political Science</i> found that immigrants in Norway became more politically engaged the earlier that they were given voting rights.<sup id="cite_ref-FerwerdaFinseraas2018_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FerwerdaFinseraas2018-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2019 study in the <i>European Economic Review</i> found that language training improved the economic assimilation of immigrants in France.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_capital">Social capital</span></h2>
<p>There is some research that suggests that immigration adversely affects <a href="/wiki/Social_capital" title="Social capital">social capital</a> in the short term.<sup id="cite_ref-AlganHémet2016_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlganHémet2016-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> One study, for instance, found that "larger increases in US states' Mexican population shares correspond to larger decreases in social capital over the period" 1986–2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Levy2018_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levy2018-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> A 2017 study in the <i><a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Comparative_Economics" title="Journal of Comparative Economics">Journal of Comparative Economics</a></i> found that "individuals whose ancestors migrated from countries with higher autocracy levels are less likely to trust others and to vote in presidential elections in the U.S. The impact of autocratic culture on trust can last for at least three generations while the impact on voting disappears after one generation. These impacts on trust and voting are also significant across Europe."<sup id="cite_ref-XuJin2018_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XuJin2018-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> A 2019 study found that "humans are inclined to react negatively to threats to homogeneity... in the short term. However, these negative outcomes are compensated in the long term by the beneficial influence of intergroup contact, which alleviates initial negative influences."<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2>
<p>Research suggests that immigration has positive effects on native workers' health.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> As immigration rises, native workers are pushed into less demanding jobs, which improves native workers' health outcomes.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_265-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2018 study found that immigration to the United Kingdom "reduced waiting times for outpatient referrals and did not have significant effects on waiting times in accident and emergency departments (A&amp;E) and elective care."<sup id="cite_ref-GiuntellaNicodemo2018_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GiuntellaNicodemo2018-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> The study also found "evidence that immigration increased waiting times for outpatient referrals in more deprived areas outside of London" but that this increase disappears after 3 to 4 years.<sup id="cite_ref-GiuntellaNicodemo2018_266-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GiuntellaNicodemo2018-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2018 systemic review and meta-analysis in <i>The Lancet</i> found that migrants generally have better health than the general population.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span></h2>
<p>A 2014 study of the United Kingdom found that immigration generally reduced house prices, because natives at the top of the wage distribution respond to immigration by moving to other areas, reducing demand for housing.<sup id="cite_ref-Sá2015_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sá2015-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_crime" title="Immigration and crime">Immigration and crime</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable relarticle mainarticle selfreference noprint">This section is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Transclusion" title="Wikipedia:Transclusion">transcluded</a> from <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_crime" title="Immigration and crime">Immigration and crime</a>. <span class="plainlinks" style="font-style: normal"><span style="font-size:85%;">(<a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Immigration_and_crime&amp;action=edit">edit</a> &#124; <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Immigration_and_crime&amp;action=history">history</a>)</span></span></div>
<p><b>Immigration and crime</b> refers to perceived or actual relationships between <a href="/wiki/Crime" title="Crime">crime</a> and <a class="mw-selflink selflink">immigration</a>. The academic literature provides mixed findings for the relationship between immigration and crime worldwide, but finds for the United States that immigration either has no impact on the crime rate or that it reduces the crime rate.<sup id="cite_ref-Integration_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Integration-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:8_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:21_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:21-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:5_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NewEvidence_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewEvidence-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:6_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> A meta-analysis of 51 studies from 1994–2014 on the relationship between immigration and crime in the United States found that overall immigration reduces crime, but the relationship is very weak.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Research suggests that people tend to overestimate the relationship between immigration and criminality,<sup id="cite_ref-:37_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:37-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:5_272-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:38_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:38-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> and that the media tends to erroneously depict immigrants as particularly crime-prone.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><br />
</p><p>The over-representation of immigrants in the criminal justice systems of several countries may be due to socioeconomic factors, imprisonment for migration offenses, and racial and ethnic discrimination by police and the judicial system.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:14-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:27_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:27-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:12_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ItalyPenal_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ItalyPenal-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> The relationship between immigration and terrorism is understudied, but existing research suggests that the relationship is weak and that repression of the immigrants increases the terror risk.<sup id="cite_ref-:46_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:46-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Induce_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Induce-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> Research on the relationship between <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugee migration</a> and crime is scarce, but existing empirical evidence fails to substantiate a relationship between refugee migration and crime.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discrimination">Discrimination</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe_2">Europe</span></h3>
<p>Research suggests that police practices, such as <a href="/wiki/Racial_profiling" title="Racial profiling">racial profiling</a>, over-policing in areas populated by minorities and in-group bias may result in disproportionately high numbers of racial minorities among crime suspects in Sweden, Italy, and England and Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-:23_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:23-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HallstenSzulkin2013_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HallstenSzulkin2013-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crocitti2013_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crocitti2013-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:29_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:29-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Parmar2013_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parmar2013-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> Research also suggests that there may be possible discrimination by the judicial system, which contributes to a higher number of convictions for racial minorities in Sweden, the Netherlands, Italy, Germany, Denmark and France.<sup id="cite_ref-:23_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:23-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crocitti2013_291-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crocitti2013-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:29_292-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:29-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HolmbergKyvsgaard2011_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HolmbergKyvsgaard2011-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RochéGordon2013_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RochéGordon2013-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Light2016_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Light2016-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WerminkJohnson2015_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WerminkJohnson2015-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> A 2018 study found that the Dutch are less likely to reciprocate in games played with immigrants than the native Dutch.<sup id="cite_ref-CettolinSuetens2018_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CettolinSuetens2018-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several meta-analyses find extensive evidence of ethnic and racial discrimination in hiring in the North-American and European labor markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Rich2014_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rich2014-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ZschirntRuedin2016_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZschirntRuedin2016-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RiachRich2002_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RiachRich2002-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> A 2016 meta-analysis of 738 correspondence tests in 43 separate studies conducted in OECD countries between 1990 and 2015 finds that there is extensive racial discrimination in hiring decisions in Europe and North-America.<sup id="cite_ref-ZschirntRuedin2016_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZschirntRuedin2016-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Equivalent minority candidates need to send around 50% more applications to be invited for an interview than majority candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-ZschirntRuedin2016_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZschirntRuedin2016-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2014 meta-analysis found extensive evidence of racial and ethnic discrimination in the housing market of several European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Rich2014_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rich2014-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_United_States">The United States</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Business">Business</span></h4>
<p>A 2014 meta-analysis of racial discrimination in product markets found extensive evidence of minority applicants being quoted higher prices for products.<sup id="cite_ref-Rich2014_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rich2014-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> A 1995 study found that car dealers "quoted significantly lower prices to white males than to black or female test buyers using identical, scripted bargaining strategies."<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> A 2013 study found that eBay sellers of iPods received 21 percent more offers if a white hand held the iPod in the photo than a black hand.<sup id="cite_ref-DoleacStein2013_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DoleacStein2013-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_justice_system">Criminal justice system</span></h4>
<p>Research suggests that police practices, such as <a href="/wiki/Racial_profiling" title="Racial profiling">racial profiling</a>, over-policing in areas populated by minorities and in-group bias may result in disproportionately high numbers of racial minorities among crime suspects.<sup id="cite_ref-WarrenTomaskovic-Devey2009_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WarrenTomaskovic-Devey2009-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MoJ_p._8_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoJ_p._8-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:53_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:53-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Donohue_IIILevitt2001_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Donohue_IIILevitt2001-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> Research also suggests that there may be possible discrimination by the judicial system, which contributes to a higher number of convictions for racial minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-AbramsBertrand2012_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AbramsBertrand2012-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mustard2001_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mustard2001-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AnwarBayer2012_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnwarBayer2012-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DaudistelHosch1999_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DaudistelHosch1999-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DepewEren2017_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DepewEren2017-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> A 2012 study found that "(i) juries formed from all-white jury pools convict black defendants significantly (16 percentage points) more often than white defendants, and (ii) this gap in conviction rates is entirely eliminated when the jury pool includes at least one black member."<sup id="cite_ref-AnwarBayer2012_308-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnwarBayer2012-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> Research has found evidence of in-group bias, where "black (white) juveniles who are randomly assigned to black (white) judges are more likely to get incarcerated (as opposed to being placed on probation), and they receive longer sentences."<sup id="cite_ref-DepewEren2017_310-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DepewEren2017-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> In-group bias has also been observed when it comes to traffic citations, as black and white cops are more likely to cite out-groups.<sup id="cite_ref-:53_304-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:53-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_2">Education</span></h4>
<p>A 2015 study using correspondence tests "found that when considering requests from prospective students seeking mentoring in the future, faculty were significantly more responsive to White males than to all other categories of students, collectively, particularly in higher-paying disciplines and private institutions."<sup id="cite_ref-MilkmanAkinola2015_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MilkmanAkinola2015-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to an analysis of the National Study of College Experience, elite colleges may favor minority applicants due to affirmative action policies.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2018 National Bureau of Economic Research paper found that math teachers discriminate against the children of immigrants. When the teachers were informed about negative stereotypes towards the children of immigrants, they gave higher grades to the children of immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing_2">Housing</span></h4>
<p>A 2014 meta-analysis found extensive evidence of <a href="/wiki/Housing_discrimination_in_the_United_States" title="Housing discrimination in the United States">racial discrimination in the American housing market</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rich2014_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rich2014-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Minority applicants for housing needed to make many more enquiries to view properties.<sup id="cite_ref-Rich2014_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rich2014-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Geographical steering of African-Americans in US housing remained significant.<sup id="cite_ref-Rich2014_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rich2014-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> A 2003 study finds  "evidence that agents interpret an initial housing request as an indication of a customer's preferences, but also are more likely to withhold a house from all customers when it is in an integrated suburban neighborhood (<a href="/wiki/Redlining" title="Redlining">redlining</a>). Moreover, agents' marketing efforts increase with asking price for white, but not for black, customers; blacks are more likely than whites to see houses in suburban, integrated areas (<a href="/wiki/Racial_steering" title="Racial steering">steering</a>); and the houses agents show are more likely to deviate from the initial request when the customer is black than when the customer is white. These three findings are consistent with the possibility that agents act upon the belief that some types of transactions are relatively unlikely for black customers (statistical discrimination)."<sup id="cite_ref-OndrichRoss2003_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OndrichRoss2003-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A report by the federal <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Housing_and_Urban_Development" title="United States Department of Housing and Urban Development">Department of Housing and Urban Development</a> where the department sent African-Americans and whites to look at apartments found that African-Americans were shown fewer apartments to rent and houses for sale.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_market">Labor market</span></h4>
<p>Several meta-analyses find extensive evidence of ethnic and racial discrimination in hiring in the American labor market.<sup id="cite_ref-Rich2014_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rich2014-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RiachRich2002_299-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RiachRich2002-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ZschirntRuedin2016_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZschirntRuedin2016-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A 2016 meta-analysis of 738 correspondence tests – tests where identical CVs for stereotypically black and white names were sent to employers – in 43 separate studies conducted in OECD countries between 1990 and 2015 finds that there is extensive racial discrimination in hiring decisions in Europe and North-America.<sup id="cite_ref-ZschirntRuedin2016_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZschirntRuedin2016-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> These correspondence tests showed that equivalent minority candidates need to send around 50% more applications to be invited for an interview than majority candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-ZschirntRuedin2016_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZschirntRuedin2016-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BertrandMullainathan2004_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BertrandMullainathan2004-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> A study that examine the job applications of actual people provided with identical résumés and similar interview training showed that African-American applicants with no criminal record were offered jobs at a rate as low as white applicants who had criminal records.<sup id="cite_ref-PagerBonikowski2009_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PagerBonikowski2009-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_on_the_sending_country">Impact on the sending country</span></h2>
<p>Remittances increase living standards in the country of origin. Remittances are a large share of the GDP of many developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Ratha_2012_1–3_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ratha_2012_1–3-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ratha_2012_1–3_318-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ratha_2012_1–3-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> A study on remittances to Mexico found that remittances lead to a substantial increase in the availability of public services in Mexico, surpassing government spending in some localities.<sup id="cite_ref-AdidaGirod2010_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AdidaGirod2010-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research finds that emigration and low migration barriers has net positive effects on human capital formation in the sending countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Shrestha2017_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shrestha2017-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BeineDocquier2008_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeineDocquier2008-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DinkelmanMariotti2016_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinkelmanMariotti2016-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BatistaLacuesta2012_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BatistaLacuesta2012-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> This means that there is a "brain gain" instead of a "brain drain" to emigration.
</p><p>One study finds that sending countries benefit indirectly in the long-run on the emigration of skilled workers because those skilled workers are able to innovate more in developed countries, which the sending countries are able to benefit on as a positive <a href="/wiki/Externality" title="Externality">externality</a>. Greater emigration of skilled workers consequently leads to greater economic growth and welfare improvements in the long-run.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> The negative effects of high-skill emigration remain largely unfounded. According to economist Michael Clemens, it has not been shown that restrictions on high-skill emigration reduce shortages in the countries of origin.<sup id="cite_ref-Clemens2015_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clemens2015-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research also suggests that emigration, remittances and return migration can have a positive impact on political institutions and democratization in the country of origin.<sup id="cite_ref-DocquierLodigiani2016_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DocquierLodigiani2016-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Escribà-FolchMeseguer2015_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Escribà-FolchMeseguer2015-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BatistaVicente2011_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BatistaVicente2011-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Escribà-FolchMeseguer2018_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Escribà-FolchMeseguer2018-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> Research also shows that remittances can lower the risk of civil war in the country of origin.<sup id="cite_ref-ReganFrank2014_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReganFrank2014-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup> Return migration from countries with liberal gender norms has been associated with the transfer of liberal gender norms to the home country.<sup id="cite_ref-TuccioWahba2018_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TuccioWahba2018-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research suggests that emigration causes an increase in the wages of those who remain in the country of origin. A 2014 survey of the existing literature on emigration finds that a 10 percent emigrant supply shock would increase wages in the sending country by 2–5.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-Mishra2014_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mishra2014-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> A study of emigration from Poland shows that it led to a slight increase in wages for high- and medium-skilled workers for remaining Poles.<sup id="cite_ref-DustmannFrattini2015_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DustmannFrattini2015-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> A 2013 study finds that emigration from Eastern Europe after the 2004 EU enlargement increased the wages of remaining young workers in the country of origin by 6%, while it had no effect on the wages of old workers.<sup id="cite_ref-Elsner2013_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsner2013-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> The wages of Lithuanian men increased as a result of post-EU enlargement emigration.<sup id="cite_ref-Elsner2012_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsner2012-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup> Return migration is associated with greater household firm revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some research shows that the remittance effect is not strong enough to make the remaining natives in countries with high emigration flows better off.<sup id="cite_ref-di_GiovanniLevchenko2015_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-di_GiovanniLevchenko2015-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
